Proof Against Tawallud: The Ahl al-Haqq Argument
Nasafi presents the Ahl al-Haqq proof that effects cannot be the act of the agent of the cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Haqq proof against the Mu'tazilite doctrine of tawallud, focusing on why a single power cannot relate to multiple objects and why a separate power would undermine causality.

Core Idea
Generated effects cannot be human acts because no created power can produce them.

This dense passage from Nasafi presents a key Sunni argument against the Mu'tazilite theory of generated acts (tawallud). The proof uses a logical disjunction: if an effect after a cause were the human agent's act, then either the agent has power over it or not, and either the same power as the cause's or another. Each possibility is shown impossible. We will unpack this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Nasafi begins by referencing earlier proofs that only God has the power of invention (ikhtira'). This establishes that human acts are mere acquisition (kasb), not creation. Keep this in mind as the foundation.
The argument builds on the prior rejection of human creative power.
2
Set up the dichotomy
The main argument starts: if the effect after a cause were the act of the agent of the cause, we ask whether the agent has power over it. If not, it cannot be his act. If yes, which power?
3
Examine the 'same power' possibility
If the same power that caused the cause also causes the effect, the text gives two reasons why this is impossible: (1) a single originated power can only relate to one object; (2) the power (e.g., the power to strike) precedes the effect (pain), but an originated power cannot precede its object.
Reason 2 is crucial: power must coexist with its object, but here it would exist before.
4
Examine the 'different power' possibility
If a different power causes the effect, the agent could produce it without the cause, and could produce its opposite. This contradicts the dependence of the effect on the cause and the known impossibility of such control (e.g., stopping an arrow after release).
This shows the effect is independent of human power, so it must be from God.
5
Understand the conclusion
The argument demonstrates that the effect cannot be the act of the human agent. Therefore, tawallud is negated. The effect is created by God while the human agent is merely the locus of the cause.
The text ends abruptly, but the reasoning is sufficient to show the intended conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل أهل الحق على نفي التولد: ودليلنا في المسألة ما سبق من الدلائل التي تدل على أن ثبوت قدرة الاختراع لغير الله تعالى محال فإن الاكتساب لذاتها لما يقوم بمحل قدرته لما يوجب إثبات قدرته على اختراع شيء وتعلقها بما ليس في محل قدرته إبطال دلالة التمانع التي هي دلالة توحيد الصانع جل وعلا، وذلك دليل كاف. ثم نقول : إن الحادث في المحل عقيب السبب لو كان فعلاً لفاعل السبب، لكان لا يخلو؛ إما أن كانت له عليه قدرة، وإما أن لم تكن عليه قدرة، فإن لم تكن تعلقت قدرته به فلا يكون فعلاً له، وإن تعلقت قدرته به لكان لا يخلو إما أن تعلقت به القدرة التي تعلقت بالسبب، وإما أن تعلقت به قدرة أخرى، ولا وجه إلى أن يقال تعلقت به عين هذه القدرة لوجهين: أحدهما: أن تعلق قدرة واحدة محدثة بمقدورين متجانسين أو متضادين أو مختلفين محال إذ كل قدرة محدثه لا تتعلق إلا بمقدور واحد، وكذا كل علم محدث أكثر أصحابنا لا يتعلق إلا بمعلوم واحد. والوجه الثاني: أن القدرة على الضرب سابقة على الألم وقوة الرمي سابقة على مرور السهم والإصابة والجرح والآلام والموت، وقد مر أن سبق القدرة المحدثة على المقدور محال ولا وجه أن يقال بأن ذلك المعنى يوجد بقدرة سوى قدرة سببه هي قدرة عليها، لأنه لو كان كذلك لما كان ذلك المعنى في المحل حاصلاً عن السبب المتقدم، ولكان القادر ممكنا من تحصيله بلا تحصيل السبب كما يقدر على تحصيل كل كسب له في حيز قدرته من غير تقدم سبب، وحيث استحال ذلك دل أنه لم يقدر عليه بقدرة هي قدرة عليه على الخصوص، ولأنه لو حصل بقدرة أخرى لصلح أن يقدر على ضده بدلاً عنه وقت وجوده بعين تلك القدرة على قول من يقول : إن الاستطاعة تصلح للضدين وبقدرة سوى هذه بدلاً عنها صالحة لضده، وحيث استحال أن يوصف بالقدرة على تسكين السهم أو الحجر بعد الرمي أو الإرسال وتخليق اللذة في بدن المضروب والمجروح بعد الضرب
The proof of the People of Truth on negating tawallud: Our proof in this matter is what has preceded of the proofs that demonstrate that establishing the power of invention (qudrat al-ikhtira') for other than God Almighty is impossible. For acquisition (iktisab) in its essence, since it subsists in the subject of his power, necessitates establishing his power over inventing something, and its relation to what is not in the locus of his power would invalidate the evidence of mutual preclusion (tamānu'), which is the evidence of the oneness of the Maker, Exalted and Mighty. And that is a sufficient proof. Then we say: The event in the locus after the cause, if it were an act of the agent of the cause, would not be free from either he has power over it or he does not have power over it. If his power does not relate to it, then it is not his act. And if his power relates to it, then it would not be free from either the power that related to the cause relates to it, or another power relates to it. And there is no way to say that the very same power relates to it for two reasons: One: that the relation of a single originated power to two objects (maqdūrayn), whether homogeneous, opposite, or different, is impossible, for every originated power relates only to one object. Similarly, every originated knowledge (according to most of our scholars) relates only to one object. The second reason: that the power over striking precedes the pain, and the force of shooting precedes the arrow's passage, hitting, wounding, pains, and death. And it has been mentioned that the precedence of an originated power over its object is impossible. And there is no way to say that that meaning (effect) exists by a power other than the power of its cause, which is a power over it, because if that were the case, that meaning would not in the locus result from the preceding cause, and the agent would be capable of producing it without producing the cause, just as he is capable of producing every acquisition (kash) of his within the domain of his power without the precedence of a cause. And since that is impossible, it indicates that he is not empowered over it by a power that is specifically a power over it. And because if it occurred by another power, he would be capable of bringing about its opposite instead of it at the time of its existence by that very same power, according to the view that capability (istitā'a) is valid for opposites, and by a power other than this to replace it, valid for its opposite. And since it is impossible to describe him as having power to still the arrow or stone after shooting or releasing, and to create pleasure in the body of the struck or wounded after striking...
Source pages p. 946

Commentary
This passage contains the proof of Ahl al-Haqq against the Mu'tazilite doctrine of tawallud (generation of effects). The proof begins by referencing earlier proofs that establish that the power of invention (qudrat al-ikhtira') belongs only to God. Then it presents a new argument: If the effect occurring after a cause were the act of the agent of the cause, we consider two possibilities. First, if the agent has no power over the effect, it cannot be his act. Second, if he does have power over it, then either it is the same power that acted on the cause, or a different power. The argument denies the first possibility (same power) for two reasons: (1) a single originated power cannot relate to two distinct objects (whether similar, opposite, or different). (2) The power over the cause (e.g., striking) exists before the effect (pain), but an originated power cannot precede its object (since it would need to exist before the act, which is impossible). Therefore, the same power cannot cause the effect. The second possibility (a different power) is also impossible because then the effect would not be dependent on the cause; the agent could produce it directly without the cause, which contradicts the notion of tawallud. Furthermore, if the effect were by a different power, the agent could produce its opposite instead at the same time, which is also impossible. The passage concludes by asserting the impossibility of describing the agent as having power over the effect after the cause (like stopping an arrow after release). The text appears incomplete, but the argument aims to show that tawallud is impossible.

اختراع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument denies all human responsibility for actions.
Correction: The argument only denies that generated effects (tawallud) are directly attributable to the human agent. It does not deny human acquisition (kasb) or responsibility for the original act (e.g., striking). The effect is created by God while the human is accountable for the cause.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why can't a single originated power relate to two objects?
A) Because two objects are contradictory.
B) Because each originated power relates only to one object.
C) Because the agent's will cannot be split.
D) Because effects are caused by God alone.

Key Takeaway
The Ahl al-Haqq proof uses logical impossibility to show that effects following a cause cannot be the act of the human agent; they are created by God directly.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every effect in your life—every pain, every success, every consequence—is directly created by Allah, not by your own power? How would living with this belief change your reaction to failure or suffering? Will you consciously remind yourself today that your acts are only acquisitions and that the outcomes are from Him alone?
?
If you have no power to generate the effects of your actions, why do you still feel responsible for them? Examine your heart: is there a hidden pride that assumes you control your results? How can you embrace the doctrine of kasb to cultivate true tawakkul, surrendering outcomes to Allah while continuing to act?
?
When you cause harm—by word or deed—do you feel guilty for the pain you caused? This passage says the pain is not your act, but your act of striking or speaking is your acquisition. Does that reduce your responsibility? No—it shifts the focus to your intent and the act itself, not the uncontrollable effect. Will you repent for the act, not just the outcome, and trust Allah’s justice in the consequences?

Causality and Created Things

Can an Effect Occur After the Agent's Death?
Imam Nasafi refutes the claim that human actions produce effects after the agent's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why, according to Maturidi kalam, effects that occur after the agent's death cannot be attributed to the agent's power.

Core Idea
A single human power cannot produce effects separated in time from its act.

Imam Nasafi now tackles a key objection from those who claim that human actions produce effects even after the agent has died, such as pain after a blow or an arrow hitting after the archer's death. This challenge, if valid, would undermine the Maturidi position that all actual effects are directly from God. Nasafi systematically dismantles the possibility through a series of logical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dichotomy
Read the opening two lines where Nasafi sets up the essential dichotomy: either the agent has power over the effect or not. If not, it's not his act. If yes, then further analysis follows.
This framing is the backbone of the whole argument.
2
Examine the first possibility: same power
Nasafi gives two reasons why the same power that acted on the cause cannot also act on the effect. Identify these reasons: (1) a single originated power can only relate to one object of power; (2) power must be simultaneous with its object.
The simultaneity principle was established earlier in the text.
3
Explore the second possibility: another power
Read the section where Nasafi argues against a separate power over the effect. He shows it would disconnect the effect from the cause and lead to absurdities like being able to produce the opposite effect at the same time.
4
Follow the thought experiments
Nasafi uses two examples: (1) if a person could produce movement in a distant body without connection, he could do so anywhere; (2) an archer who dies before the arrow hits would have performed a precise act without power, knowledge, or life. Both are impossible.
These illustrate the absurd consequences of the opponent's position.
5
Conclude and reflect
The conclusion is that the agent has no power over such effects at all. Reflect on how this upholds the Maturidi doctrine of direct divine causation for all actual events.
This refutation protects tawhid in actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يخلو؛ إما أن كانت له عليه قدرة، وإما أن لم تكن عليه قدرة، فإن لم تكن تعلقت قدرته به فلا يكون فعلاً له، وإن تعلقت قدرته به لكان لا يخلو إما أن تعلقت به القدرة التي تعلقت بالسبب، وإما أن تعلقت به قدرة أخرى، ولا وجه إلى أن يقال تعلقت به عين هذه القدرة لوجهين: أحدهما: أن تعلق قدرة واحدة محدثة بمقدورين متجانسين أو متضادين أو مختلفين محال إذ كل قدرة محدثه لا تتعلق إلا بمقدور واحد، وكذا كل علم محدث أكثر أصحابنا لا يتعلق إلا بمعلوم واحد. والوجه الثاني: أن القدرة على الضرب سابقة على الألم وقوة الرمي سابقة على مرور السهم والإصابة والجرح والآلام والموت، وقد مر أن سبق القدرة المحدثة على المقدور محال ولا وجه أن يقال بأن ذلك المعنى يوجد بقدرة أخرى سوى قدرة سببه هي قدرة عليها، لأنه لو كان كذلك لما كان ذلك المعنى في المحل حاصلاً عن السبب المتقدم، ولكان القادر ممكنا من تحصيله بلا تحصيل السبب كما يقدر على تحصيل كل كسب له في حيز قدرته من غير تقدم سبب، وحيث استحال ذلك دل أنه لم يقدر عليه بقدرة هي قدرة عليه على الخصوص، ولأنه لو حصل بقدرة أخرى لصلح أن يقدر على ضده بدلاً عنه وقت وجوده بعين تلك القدرة على قول من يقول: إن الاستطاعة تصلح للضدين وبقدرة سوى هذه بدلاً عنها صالحة لضده، وحيث استحال أن يوصف بالقدرة على تسكين السهم أو الحجر بعد الرمي أو الإرسال وتخليق اللذة في بدن المضروب والمجروح بعد الضرب والجرح وتحصيل الحياة بعد الجرح الفاحش بدلاً عن الموت؛ دل أنه لا يجوز أن يقدر عليه بقدرة خاصة له ولأنه لو قدر على إيجاد حركة أو سكون في جسم يقرب منه من غير اعتماد عليه واتصال به لقدر أن يفعل ذلك في جسم ببغداد وهو ببخارى، أو جسم بأقصى المغرب، ولصحت قدرته على إيجاد ذلك في أي شاء وذلك ظاهر الفساد، وإذا بطل أن يكون قادرًا على ذلك المعنى بقدرة سببه وبقدرة أخرى سواها بطل أن يكون قادرًا عليه أصلاً، ولأنا نعلم جواز موت الرامي بعد رميه قبل الإصابة وبعدما مات لا يتصور منه قدرة ولا علم، فلو كان ما يوجد من الأفعال بعد ذلك أفعالاً له وهي محكمة متقنه لجاز خلو كل فعل محكم عن قدرة فاعله وعلمه وحياته ولجاز حصوله بموات عاجز جاهل، وقد مر هذا، والله الموفق. شبه الخصوم واهية
It cannot be otherwise: either he had power over it, or he did not have power over it. If his power was not related to it, then it is not his act. If his power was related to it, then it cannot be otherwise: either the power that was related to the cause was related to it, or another power was related to it. There is no way to say that the very same power was related to it, for two reasons: One of them is that the relation of a single originated power to two objects of power, whether homogeneous, opposite, or different, is impossible, because every originated power is related only to one object of power, and similarly, according to most of our companions, every originated knowledge is related only to one object of knowledge. The second reason: that power over striking precedes pain, and the force of shooting precedes the passage of the arrow, hitting, wounding, pains, and death. It has already passed that the precedence of an originated power over the object of power is impossible. And there is no way to say that that meaning comes into existence by another power besides the power of its cause, that is a power over it, because if it were so, then that meaning in the locus would not be produced from the preceding cause, and the agent would be able to produce it without producing the cause, just as he is able to produce every acquisition of his in the sphere of his power without a preceding cause. And since that is impossible, it indicates that he does not have power over it by a power that is a power over it specifically. And because if it were produced by another power, it would be valid for him to have power over its opposite instead of it at the time of its existence by that very same power, according to the one who says that capacity is valid for opposites, and by another power instead of this one valid for its opposite. And since it is impossible for him to be described as having power to calm the arrow or stone after shooting or releasing, and to create pleasure in the body of the struck and wounded after striking and wounding, and to produce life after a fatal wound instead of death, it indicates that it is not permissible for him to have power over it by a specific power of his. And because if he had power to produce movement or rest in a body near him without dependence on it and connection to it, then he would have power to do that to a body in Baghdad while he is in Bukhara, or a body in the far West, and his power to produce that in whatever he wishes would be valid, and that is clearly corrupt. And if it is invalid that he is powerful over that meaning by the power of its cause and by another power besides it, then it is invalid that he is powerful over it at all. And because we know the possibility of the archer's death after his shooting before the hitting, and after he dies, power and knowledge cannot be conceived from him. So if what occurs of actions after that were his actions and they are firm and precise, then it would be permissible for every firm action to be devoid of the power, knowledge, and life of its doer, and it would be permissible for it to be produced by a dead, incapable, ignorant thing. And this has already passed. And Allah is the Granter of success. The illusions of the opponents are weak.
Source pages p. 947

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the opponents' claim that an effect which occurs after the agent's death (e.g., pain after a blow, or an arrow hitting after the shooter dies) is still an act of that agent. Imam Nasafi presents a rigorous argument to show that such effects cannot be attributed to human power. He begins by setting up a dichotomy: either the agent has power over the effect or not. If not, it is not his act. If he does, then either the same power that acted on the cause also acts on the effect, or a different power does. The first option is impossible for two reasons: (1) a single originated power cannot relate to two distinct objects of power—this is a fundamental principle of kalam; (2) power must be simultaneous with its effect, but the power over the cause (e.g., striking) precedes the effect (pain), and precedence of power over its object is impossible. The second option—another power—is also impossible because if there were a separate power over the effect, then the effect would not be causally linked to the original action, and the agent could produce the effect without performing the cause, which is absurd. Moreover, if a different power existed, the agent would be able to produce the opposite of the effect at that same time, which is not observed (e.g., one cannot calm an arrow after it is shot). This leads to the conclusion that the agent has no power over such effects at all. Nasafi then strengthens the argument with a thought experiment: if a person could produce movement in a distant body without connection, he could do so anywhere, which is absurd. Finally, he cites the example of an archer who dies before the arrow hits: if the hitting were his action, then a dead person would be performing a precise act without power, knowledge, or life—an impossibility. Thus, the opponents' position is refuted. The passage follows the standard Maturidi methodology of proving that all actual effects are directly from God's power, not from created powers that are temporally separated from their effects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a person is still responsible for effects that occur after death, such as an arrow hitting after the archer dies.
Correction: This passage shows that such effects cannot be attributed to human power because power must be simultaneous with its object, and a dead person cannot have power or knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, why cannot a single originated power be related to two different objects of power?
A) Because the objects would be contradictory.
B) Because every originated power is related only to one object of power.
C) Because the power would be divided.
D) Because the objects are simultaneous.

Key Takeaway
Effects that occur after the agent's death cannot be attributed to human power because power must be simultaneous with its object, and any attribution leads to logical absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that your actions 'speak for themselves' or that their consequences continue to be 'yours' even when you are no longer involved? How does this passage challenge you to reconsider what truly belongs to your agency?
?
This lesson shows that human power is strictly limited to the moment and object. When you think about your own abilities, do you tend to overestimate your control over outcomes? What is one area where you need to humble yourself and acknowledge that only Allah’s power is continuous?
?
The argument refutes the idea that a dead person can be the agent of actions. How does this affect your view of the afterlife and the fact that all deeds will be accounted for only while alive? Are you living today with the urgency that your power is only for this moment?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
8 min
Refuting Posthumous Attribution of Actions
Refutes attribution of actions after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why actions occurring after an agent's death cannot be attributed to that agent, based on the necessity of power and life for agency.

Core Idea
An agent's capacity ceases at death; posthumous effects cannot be his actions.

This passage presents a rational argument from Nasafi's Tabirat al-Adilla: a person cannot be the agent of an action after death because agency requires power and life. Using the example of an archer who dies before his arrow strikes, the author eliminates all possible attributions and concludes that the arrow's flight cannot be the archer's act after his death. This refutes the claim that an agent's intention before death suffices to make him responsible for posthumous effects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the logical flow: a general argument about power over distance, then the archer example, then a quote from al-Khayyat enumerating four possibilities.
2
Identify the core thesis
Identify that the author is refuting the idea that actions after death can be attributed to the deceased. The key point is that after death, the agent has no power or knowledge.
3
Examine the four possibilities
Focus on al-Khayyat's enumeration of four possibilities for the arrow's flight: act of God, act of the arrow, act with no agent, or act of the archer. Understand why each except the archer's original action while alive is invalid.
4
Reflect on theological implications
Consider why this matters: if posthumous attribution were allowed, it would imply that a solid action can occur without a capable agent, which is absurd. This underscores that agency requires the agent's existence and capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجرح وتحصيل الحياة بعد الجرح الفاحش بدلاً عن الموت؛ دل أنه لا يجوز أن يقدر عليه بقدرة خاصة له ولأنه لو قدر على إيجاد حركة أو سكون في جسم يقرب منه من غير اعتماد عليه واتصال به لقدر أن يفعل ذلك في جسم ببغداد وهو ببخارى، أو جسم بأقصى المغرب، ولصحت قدرته على إيجاد ذلك في أي شاء وذلك ظاهر الفساد، وإذا بطل أن يكون قادرًا على ذلك المعنى بقدرة سببه وبقدرة أخرى سواها بطل أن يكون قادرًا عليه أصلاً، ولأنا نعلم جواز موت الرامي بعد رميه قبل الإصابة وبعدما مات لا يتصور منه قدرة ولا علم، فلو كان ما يوجد من الأفعال بعد ذلك أفعالاً له وهي محكمة متقنه لجاز خلو كل فعل محكم عن قدرة فاعله وعلمه وحياته ولجاز حصوله بموات عاجز جاهل، وقد مر هذا، والله الموفق. شبه الخصوم واهية. يقول في هذا الخياط ردًا على ابن الراوندي: إن أراد الأحياء القادرين على الأفعال يفعلون في حال حياتهم أفعالاً تتولد عنها أفعال بعد موتهم فينسب ما يتولد عن أفعالهم بعد موتهم إليهم إذا كانوا قد سنوه في حياتهم وفعلوا ما أوجبه .. وذلك كرجل أرسل حجرًا من رأس جبل فهي إلى الأرض ثم إن الله أمات المرسل للحجر قبل أن يصل الحجر إلى الأرض فنقول: إن هوى الحجر بعد موت المرسل متولد عن إرساله إياه فهو منسوب إليه دون ... وكذلك نقول في رجل نزع قوسه يريد الهدف فلما خرج السهم عن قوسه أمات الله .امي. فنقول إن ذهاب السهم بعد الرامي متولد عن رميته فهو منسوب إليه. والدليل على ذلك أن ذهاب السهم عند رمي الرامي به لا يعدو خصالاً أربعا إما أن يكون فعلا الله أو للسهم أو فعلا لا فاعل له، أو فعلا للرامي. وليس يجوز أن يكون فعلا الله، لأن الرامي لا يدخل الله في أفعاله لأن الله مختار لأفعاله، ولا يجوز أن يكون ذهاب السهم فعلاً للسهم لأن السهم موات ليس بحي ولا قادر ولا يجوز أن يكون ذهاب السهم فعلا لا فاعل له، لأن ذلك لو جاز لجاز كتاب لا كاتب له. فلما فسدت هذه الوجوه لم يبق إلا ذهاب السهم منسوب إلى الرامي به دون غيره إذ كان هو المسبب له راجع الانتصار للخياط ص ٦٠-٦١.
And the wound and the acquisition of life after a severe wound instead of death indicates that it is not permissible that he be capable of it by a power specific to him, and because if he were capable of producing a movement or stillness in a body near him without depending on it or being connected to it, he would be capable of doing that to a body in Baghdad while he is in Bukhara, or to a body in the farthest Maghreb, and his power would be valid to produce that in whichever he wills, and that is clearly corrupt. And if it is false that he be capable of that meaning by a power of its cause and by another power besides it, it becomes false that he be capable of it at all. And because we know the permissibility of the archer's death after his shot before the hitting, and after he dies, no power or knowledge can be conceived from him. So if what exists of actions after that were his actions, and they are precise and solid, then it would be permissible for every solid action to be devoid of the power, knowledge, and life of its agent, and it would be permissible for it to come about from a lifeless, incapable, ignorant thing. This has already passed. And God is the success. The dubious arguments of the opponents are weak. Al-Khayyat says in response to Ibn al-Rawandi: The living, capable of actions do actions in their life from which actions are generated after their death, so what is generated from their actions after their death is attributed to them if they had established it in their life and did what necessitated it. That is like a man who threw a stone from the top of a mountain, and it fell to the ground, then God caused the sender to die before the stone reached the ground. We say: The fall of the stone after the death of the sender is generated from his sending it, so it is attributed to him... Similarly, we say about a man who drew his bow aiming at the target, and when the arrow left his bow, God caused him to die. We say: The flight of the arrow after the archer is generated from his shooting, so it is attributed to him. And the proof of that is that the flight of the arrow upon the archer's shooting it does not go beyond four possibilities: either it is an act of God, or of the arrow, or an act with no agent, or an act of the archer. It is not permissible that it be an act of God, because the archer does not involve God in his actions, as God is independent in His actions. And it is not permissible that the flight of the arrow be an act of the arrow, because the arrow is lifeless, not alive nor capable. And it is not permissible that the flight of the arrow be an act with no agent, because if that were permissible, a book without a writer would be permissible. So when these possibilities are invalidated, nothing remains except that the flight of the arrow is attributed to the archer, not to others, since he is its cause. Refer to al-Intisar of al-Khayyat, pp. 60-61.
Source pages p. 948

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that actions occurring after the agent's death can be attributed to the agent. The author begins by presenting a proof: If a person could produce movement or stillness in a body near him without direct contact, he could also do so in a distant body, which is absurd. Therefore, power cannot be transferred or extended after death. Then the author uses the example of an archer: It is possible for the archer to die before his arrow hits the target. After death, he has no power or knowledge. If the arrow's flight after death were his action, then every precise action could be without a capable agent, which is absurd. The passage then includes a quote from al-Khayyat arguing in detail that the arrow's flight is generated from the archer's action and thus attributed to him, enumerating four possibilities and eliminating all but the attribution to the archer. The overall argument is that actions after death cannot be the agent's act because his capacity ceases at death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that an intention before death suffices to attribute posthumous effects to the agent.
Correction: The author shows that the agent's capacity ceases at death; no power or knowledge remains, so posthumous effects cannot be his acts.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why can the flight of an arrow after the archer's death not be attributed to the archer?
A) Because the arrow is lifeless.
B) Because the archer has no power or knowledge after death.
C) Because God creates the flight directly.
D) Because the arrow moves by its own nature.

Key Takeaway
The argument proves that an agent's actions require his power and life; after death, no power remains, so posthumous effects cannot be attributed to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are alive right now with power to act. This passage argues that your capacity ends at death. What actions are you postponing that you assume you will have time later to complete? How does this urgent reality change your plan for today?
?
Consider the archer: he died before the arrow hit. Are there outcomes in your life that you think will be credited to you after you are gone? The passage says your actions end at death. How can you ensure that your current deeds have lasting effect without relying on future credit?
?
The passage refutes the idea that you can be the agent of an event after your death. Is there an event you hope will occur after your death to vindicate you or prove your intentions? How does this teaching free you from needing posthumous justification?
